The O-RU8 shall ensure that a persistent connection to any NETCONF client with “sudo” privileges is maintained by 1 
actively testing t he aliveness of the connection using the keep -alive mechanism defined in [15]. The establishment of 2 
NETCONF client privileges is covered in Section 3.4. 3 
A3.3.5 SSH Connection Establishment 4 
The identity of the SSH server ( O-RU8) shall be verified and authenticated  by the SSH client (NETCONF client) 5 
according to local policy before password- based authentication data or any configuration or state data is sent to or 6 
received from the SSH server.  7 
Public key-based host authentication shall be used for authenticating th e server (RFC 4253) by the clients. In addition, 8 
server authentication based on X.509 certificates may also be provided [31]. 9 
Note: P ublic key- based host authentication requires that the SSH server (O -RU8) public keys are provisioned in the 10 
NETCONF client (e.g., O-DU8). As an alternative, RFC4251 mentions that “a possible strategy is to only accept a host 11 
key without checking the first time a host is connected, save the key in a local database, and compare against that key 12 
on all future connections to that host.”. This option simplifies the key management procedure as it doesn’t require to 13 
pre-populate them in O -DU8 / NMS (SSH client) bu t obviously at the price of degraded security, therefore the support 14 
of this option shall be configurable and left to operator’s choice. 15 
A3.3.5.1 NETCONF Security 16 
In this version of O -RU8 Management Plane Specification, the security of the NETCONF protocol is reali zed using 17 
SSHv2. O -RAN NETCONF implementations shall implement RFC 6242 [5] that addresses earlier delimiter issues 18 
when using RFC 4742. 19 
As the default, the NETCONF Server in the O -RU8 shall provide access to the NETCONF subsystem only when using 20 
SSH estab lished using the IANA -assigned TCP port 830 [5]. The O -RU8 may be con figured to additionally allow 21 
access to the NETCONF subsystem over other ports. 22 
If multiple NETCONF sessions are established to an O -RU8, those sessions shall be established over separate SSH 23 
tunnels. 24 
A3.3.5.2 NETCONF Authentication 25 
This version of the O -RU8 Management Plane Specification uses password authentication method for SSHv2 [6]. In 26 
addition, client authentication based on X.509 certificates may also be provided [31].  27 
Upon initial system i nitialization, the O -RU8 is configured with a default account. The specific details of the default 28 
account are to be agreed  between operator and vendor. An example of a default user account is one with username 29 
“oranuser”.  30 
The default account may be of account -type PASSWORD, in which case a default password also needs to be defined 31 
and configured in the O-RU8, for example “o-ran-password”. 32 
Note: As the default account may be operator specific, this may require that the O -RU8 provides facilities to con figure 33 
securely this default account at installation time (i.e. before the O-RU8 is connected to the O-DU8). 34 
The default account is member of the “sudo” access control group (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges) as i t 35 
can be used to create other accounts (see Section 3.3.3). 36 
The identity of the SSH client (NETCONF client) shall  be verified and authenticated by the SSH server ( O-RU8) 37 
according to local policy to ensure that the incoming SSH client request is legitimate  before any configuration or state 38 
data is sent to or received from the SSH client.  39 
Upon initial system initialization, the NETCONF client can authenticate itself to the O -RU8 using SSH Authentication, 40 
with the agreed default username and password. 41 
If authentication based on X.509 certificates according to [31] is supported by SSH client and server, the certificates 42 
need to be installed at initial system in itialization, or can be obtained through certificate enrolment with operator’s PKI 43 
(certificate enrolment as defined by 3GPP with CMPv2 protocol between the NE and the operator’s CA).  44

For the purposes of user authentication, the mapping between certificates and user names is provided by the 1 
SubjectAltName field of the X.509 certificate, which means that the user name is coded in the subjectAltName. The 2 
username is determined from the subjectAltName using the rules defined in RFC 7589.  3 
A3.3.5.3 User Account Provisioning 4 
The NETCONF client with sui table privileges may  provision user accounts on the O -RU8, including the accounts 5 
(users) name, password , group (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges)  and whether a particular account is 6 
enabled or disabled.  7 
• The username name is a string between 3 -32 characters. The first character must be a lowercase letter. The 8 
remaining characters can be a lowercase letter or a number.  9 
• The account-type is an enumeration, indicating whether password or certificate- based authentication is used for this 10 
account. 11 
• The password is a string between 8-128 characters. Allowed characters in the password field include lowercase and 12 
uppercase letters, numbers and the special characters: ! $ % ^ ( ) _ + ~ { } [ ] . –  The password leaf is not present for 13 
those user accounts associated with certificate-based authentication. 14 
• The access control group associated with an account (see Section 3.4 for details of groups/privileges). 15 
• Whether an account is enabled. The YANG model ensures that  at least one user account is always enabled on the 16 
O-RU8 17 
The new account information (user name, password, access group and whether the account is enabled) shall be stored 18 
in reset-persistent memory in O-RU8. 19 
When certificate based client authentication i s used no password needs to be provisioned. At time of SSH connection, 20 
user’s authorization is done based on the X.509 certificate’s SubjectAltName field that codes the associated account’s 21 
name. 22 
When other user account  (sudo) is created, the NETCONF clien t closes existing NETCONF session as described in 23 
section 3.7. Then, the O-RU8 disables the default account and default account stays disabled  over the resets. The default 24 
account becomes enabled when the O-RU8 is reset to the factory default software by f ollowing the procedures defined 25 
in subsection 5.7.  Any o ther way to enable the default account is not precluded as O -RU8 vendor implementation 26 
matter. 27 
A3.3.6 NETCONF Access Control 28 
This subsection provides the access control for NETCONF client. Its motivation is when multiple NETCONF clients 29 
(users) exist, access control mechanism allows to limit some operation for one client but full access for the other client.  30 
In particular, for hybrid a ccess configuration as introduced in Chapter 2, this allows the privileges associated with the 31 
NETCONF client in the O -DU8 to be distinct and different from the privileges associated with the NETCONF client in 32 
the NMS 33 
In order to support interoperable access control management, the NETCONF Server shall use the IETF NETCONF 34 
Access Control Model [RFC8341]. 35 
Currently four access control groups  are defined per SSH session: “sudo”, “nms”, “fm -pm”, and “swm”.  The table 36 
below maps the group name to different privileges. Privileges are defined per namespace for read “R”, write “W” and 37 
execute “X” rpc operations or subscribe to Notifications.  38 
Note: when operating in hybrid management, the definition of above groupings does not preclude the NETCONF  client 39 
in a centralized network management system from being configure d with “sudo” privilege s. However, importantly the 40 
operation of the O -DU8 in those situations may not be defined. For example, an O -DU8 when operating with an O -RU8 41 
which receives an au tonomous reset RPC from a centralized NMS may not result in the O -DU8 recovering the o -ran-42 
operations:operational-info/operational-state/restart-cause from the O -RU8 to then determine that an NMS 43 
triggered reset has been performed. 44

A3.3.7 NETCONF capability discovery 4 
The O-RU8 advertises its NETCONF capabilities in the NETCONF Hello message. The Hello message provides an 5 
indication of support for standard features defined in NETCONF RFCs as well as support for specific namespaces.  6 
NETCONF c apabilities are exchanged between the O -RU8 and the NETCONF client(s). Examples of capabilitie s 7 
include [3]: 8 
• Writable-running Capability 9 
• Candidate Configuration Capability and associated Commit operation 10 
• Discard change operation 11 
• Lock and un-lock operations 12 
• Confirmed commit Capability 13 
• Cancel commit operation 14 
• Rollback on error capability 15 
• Validate Capability 16 
• Startup configuration capability 17 
• URL capability 18 
• XPATH capability 19 
• Notifications 20 
• Interleave capability 21 
All O -RAN O -RU8s shall support NETCONF Notifications and at least one of the writeable -running and candidate 22 
configuration capabilities. 23 
The NETCONF client uses the get  RPC together with sub-tree based <filter> and XPATH based <filter> to recover 24 
particular sub -trees from the O -RU8. Please see Chapter 6 for more information on NETCONF based configuration 25 
management. 26 
In order to avoid interactions between the operation of supervision watchdog timer (see section 3. 6) and the confirmed 27 
commit timer (default value set to 600 seconds in RFC 6241), when using the NETCONF confirmed commit capability, 28 
a NECTONF client with “sudo” privileges shall ensure the confirmed-timeout is less than the supervision-notification-29 
interval timer (default value 60 seconds in o-ran-supervision.yang).  30 
A3.3.8 Monitoring NETCONF connectivity 31 
When having a session with a NETCONF client with “sudo” access privil eges, the O -RU8 operates a watchdog 32 
supervision timer to ensure that the session to the NECTONF client is persistent, as described in section 3.4.  33 
Additionally, the O-RU8 provides NETCONF Notifications to indicate to remote systems that its management system is 34 
operational. This supervision is intended to be used with the NETCONF client associated with the operation of the peer 35 
to the O-RAN Radio’s lower layer split. 36 
Note, if another NETCONF client is discovered or con figured, e.g., in hybrid mode of operat ion, and is used to 37 
establish a NETCONF session with “sudo” access privileges, the same watchdog supervision rules shall apply, 38 
meaning that a NETCONF server shall support the operation of individual supervision watchdog timers for each 39 
NETCONF client with “sudo” privileges . 40 

 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
110 
 
The NETCONF client is respo nsible for automatically enabling the operation of the supervision watchdog timer  by 1 
creating supervision -notification subscription, whenever the O -RU8 has an established NETCONF session to a client 2 
with “sud o” privileges. After it has been enabled, the O -RU8 is responsible for repeatedly sending supervision-3 
notification. After that NETCONF client is responsible for sending supervision-watchdog-reset RPC and server shall 4 
send next notification timestamp in rep ly. When resetting the watchdog timer, the NETCO NF client may con figure a 5 
new value for the watchdog timer.  Client can set new value of watchdog timer without receiving supervision-6 
notification from O-RU8. New value is taken into use immediately with respect to supervision-watchdog-reset RPC 7 
content. Next notification should be expected not later than at the moment addressed in timestamp provided by RPC 8 
reply. 9 
If the watchdog timer expires, the O -RU8 will enter “supervision failure” condition, as described in Chapter 11.  If all 10 
NETCONF sessions to NECTONF clients with “sudo” privileges are closed, the O -RU8 shall immediately disable 11 
operation of the supervision timer. 12

A3.3.9 Closing a NETCONF Session 4 
A NETCONF client closes an existing NETCONF session by issuing the  RPC close-session command. The O -RU8 5 
shall respond and close the SSH session. The O -RU8 shall then re -commence call home procedures, as described in 6 
Section 3.2. 7 
Note, under normal operations, it is expected that at least one NETCONF session with “sudo” p rivileges is long -lived 8 
and used to repeatedly reset the O-RU8’s supervision watchdog timer. 9 
Note, if a NETCONF client has been previously become known to an O -RU8 by being con figured using NETCONF, 10 
and the NETCONF client is subsequently removed from the O -RU8’s configuration, e.g., by a second NETCONF client 11 
with “sudo” privileges, the NETCONF server shall force the termination of the NETCONF session to the removed 12 
client.  13 
A3.4 O-RU8 to O-DU8 Interface Management  14 
An O-RU8 has a number of network interfaces, i ncluding Ethernet, VLAN and IP interfaces. This section describes the 15 
management of these network interfaces.  16 
A3.4.1 O-RU8 Interfaces 17 
The O -RU8’s configuration for its interfaces is defined usi ng the o -ran-interfaces-cpri.yang module. This module 18 
augments the st andard ietf -interfaces.yang and ietf -ip.yang modules. The base interface corresponds to the CPRI  19 
interface.  But to align the M plane specification of WG4 as much as possible, the O -RU8’s former interface 20 
informations are kept. They are built on a layering principle where each interface has a unique name.  21 
Because the o -ran-interfaces-cpri model defines augments to the ietf -interfaces model, the O -RU8 can leverage the 22 
definition of operati onal state in ietf -interfaces to optionally report packet and byte co unts on a per interface basis. A 23 
single RPC is defined in the o-ran-interfaces-cpri module, to enable these counters to be reset. 24 
A3.4.2 Transceiver 25 
The o-ran-transceiver YANG module is used to define operational state for the pluggable transceiver module (like S FP, 26 
SFP+, SFP28 , XFP and QSFP, QSFP+, QSFP28, QSFP56 ). Each transceiver is associated with a unique interface-27 
name and port-number. 28 
A digital diagnostic monitoring interface for optical transceivers is used to allow access to device operating parameters. 29 
As specified in SFF-8472 [16] and SFF-8636 [34], data is typically retrieved from the transceiver module in a file. This 30 
file may be obtained from O-RU8 by the NETCONF client. Please see Chapter 9 for more details. 31 
With QSFP form factor, the optical links m ay be multi -wavelengths (4xTx & 4xRx) and/or multi -fibers (MPO -  32 
Multifiber Parallel Optic). The QSFP digital diagnostic interface [ 34] describes the use of optical lanes and the O -RU8 33 
interface management defines alarm 29 :“transceiver fault” for all media lanes. 34 
The byte with offset i (i=0, …, 511) from the beginning of the file is the byte read from data address i of the transceiver  35 
memory at two -wire interface address 0xA0 if i<256, otherwise it is the byte read from data address i -256 of the 36 
transceiver memory at two -wire interface address 0xA2. The retrieved data is stored in the file without any conversion 37 
in binary format. 38 
The O-RU8 stores data from the transceiver module on transceiver module detection during startup. The data from  the 39 
transceiver module is saved in the file. A NETCONF client can upload it by using the File Upload procedure defined in 40 
chapter 9.  The O-RU8 does not synchronize contents of the file with transceiver memory in runtime, therefore bytes 41 
representing dynamic information are  expected to be outdated . The O-RU8 does not remove the file on transceiver 42 
module removal. If a transceiver module is inserted during File Upload procedure then the procedure may provide a file 43 
with previous content or fail (with failure reason as listed in File Upload procedure). If the O -RU8 is unable to retrieve 44 

 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
113 
 
the data from the transceiver module or it is not present then the O-RU8 does not create the file or removes the file 1 
created earlier (note that File Upload procedure requesting non-existing file shall fail).  2 
The file name shall have the following syntax: 3 
sfp_{portNumber}.sffcap 4 
where {portNumber} is the value of port -number leaf of the corresponding list of port -transceiver data. Examples: 5 
sfp_0.sffcap, sfp_1.sffcap. 6 
A3.4.3 U Plane VLAN Configuration 7 
The CPRI interface for U plane actually does not need VLAN ID,  The purpose of keeping t he VLAN ID for CPRI 8 
interface is that this VLAN ID can  be used for shared cell combination. The VLAN ID here is more like an indicator of 9 
the cell id. The O -RU8s with th e same VLAN ID represent that those O -RU8s share the same cell. By default, VLAN 10 
tagging is enabled on all interfaces. This permits an O -RU8 to autonomously discover that it is connected to a trunk 11 
port, as described in Section 3.1.2. The VLAN ID for U plane can share the same VLAN ID of the management plane. 12 
The 16 bits VLAN ID can be transmitted with the IQ data in the vender specific control words.  13 
To compatible with legacy products with defined CPRI specifications (Z .16.0~Z.16.4,and Z.80.0 ~ Z.80.4 w ere 14 
designed for other purposes), Z.144.0 and Z.144.1 two vendor specific control wor ds will be used to transfer the Vlan  15 
ID. 16 
BYTE index Function Content 
Z.16.2 MSBs of Vlan ID 8 MSBs of VLAN ID 
Z.16.3 LSBs of Vlan ID 8 LSBs of VLAN ID 
Table Annex 3-3: VLAN ID Cofiguration 17 
A3.4.4 Definition of processing elements   18 
The U -plane application need s to be uniquely associate d with specific  data flows . This association is achieved by 19 
defining an O -RU8 “processing element” which can then  be associated with a particular U  plane endpoint address or 20 
delay measurement operation. 21 
For U plane with the CPRI interface， the O-RU8 management plane supports only one option to define the processing 22 
elements. 23 
• Processing element definition based on usage of CPRI interface;  24 
A processing element defines both the  local and remote endpoints used with a specific data flow. The processing 25 
element definition includ es its element name which is then used by other systems  to refer to a particular processing 26 
element instance. 27 
The o -ran-interfaces-cpri YANG model is used to define feature support for U plane transport based on CPRI. The 28 
exchange of NETCONF capabilities i s used to signal which optional capabilities are suppor ted by the O -RU8, as 29 
described in Annex C. 30 
The o -ran-processing-element-cpri YANG model uses a processing -elements container to define the  processing 31 
elements. The processing element is identified by a unique element  name. The processing element references  a 32 
particular interface-name used to support the data flows associated with a particular processing element. Depending 33 
upon the type of U plane transport session, additionally leafs are con figured that specify MAC addresses, and/or 34 
VLANs and/or IP addresse s used to identify the  particular processing element.  The mac addresss, VLANs and/or IP 35 
adreees for the U plane can be virtually assigned as that of the management plane. 36 
A3.4.5 O-DU8 Verification of U Plane Transport Connectivity  37 
Refer to ‘Common Public Radio Interface (CPRI); Interface Specification’ [35], section 4.2.10. 38

A3.4.6 Delay Management 1 
A3.4.6.1 Delay Parameters 2 
For definition of link delay measurement, please r efer to ‘ Common Public Radio Interface (CPRI); Interface 3 
Specification’ [35] V7, section 4.2.9 and section 6.1.Time delay measurement process is described as follows: 4 
 5 
Figure Annex 3-9: Delay modul 6 
 T12 is the delay of downlink signal from the output point of REC (R1) to the input point o f RE (R2). 7 
 T34 is the delay of uplink signal from the output point of RE (R3) to the input point of REC (R4).  8 
 Toffset is the frame offset between the input signal at R2 and the output signal at R3  9 
 T14 is the frame timing difference between the output signal at R1 and the input signal at R4. 10 
 TBdelayDL is the delay of downlink signal between RB2 and RB1. 11 
 TBdelayUL is the delay of uplink signal between RB4 and RB3. 12 
 N(unit:basic frame,the difference of the frame position at RB3 relative to RB4.)  13 
 14 
A3.4.6.2 Measurement Process 15 
In the c ase of single stage or cascade, the following message process is used to complete the delay measurement 16 
configuration on any O-RU8. 17 
 18 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
115 
 
 1 
  2 
Figure Annex 3-10: Delay measurement and configuration process 3 
The following steps are described based on the delay measurement after the link (including the C&M channel) has been 4 
properly established： 5 
1) After O -RU8 receives the delay measurement request message sent by O-DU8, it reports  its delay measurement 6 
value to O-DU8 through the delay measurement response. These measurement values should include the following 7 
delay： 8 
 Toffset 9 
 T2a 10 
 Ta3 11 
 TBdelay DL 12 
 TBdelay UL 13 
 N  14 
2) O-DU8 calculated the fiber delay in the upper and lower directions according  to the time delay measurement values  15 
of all O-RU8 returned measured response message. The formula is as follows: CPRI Specification V 7 section 6.1. 16 
3) After completion of the calculation, O -DU8 calculated the required time delay compensation value of each O -RU8 17 
according to the maximum compensa tion capacity and time delay measurement results reported by each O -18 
RU8.Then, the downlink and uplinking delay measurement results, downlink and uplinking delay compensation 19 
values required by each O -RU8 and the corresponding frame timing advance were sent  to each O-RU8 through the 20 
message of delay configuration command, and the O-RU8 configuration took effect。 21 
O-RU8 notifies O-DU8 of successful delay configuration via a delay configuration command response message.  22

A3.5 Software Management 1 
The Software Management function provides a set of operations allowing the desired software build to be downloaded, 2 
installed and activated at O -RU8. Successful software activation operation does not mean an O -RU8 is running the just 3 
activated software build. An O -RU8 reset RPC is required to trigger the O -RU8 to take the activated software build into 4 
operational use. 5 
A single software build is conside red as set of internally consistent files compliant within such a build. Replacement of 6 
files within a build is prohibited, as this will cause software version incompatibility. Software build is a subject of 7 
versioning and maintenance and as such cannot be broken. 8 
The use of compression and ciphering for the content of the software build is left  to vendor implementation . The only 9 
file which shall never be ciphered is the manifest.xml file.  10 
It is also Vendor's responsibility to handle SW Build / package / file integrity check. 11 
The O-RU8 provides a set of so called "software slots" or "slots". Eac h slot provides an independent storage location for 12 
a single software build. The number of slots offered by O -RU8 depends on the device’s capabilities. At least two 13 
writable slots shall be available at the O -RU8 for failsafe update operation. Presence of r ead only slot is optional. The 14 
software slots are resources provided by the O -RU8 and as such are not the subject of creation and deletion. The size of 15 
individual software slots is fixed and determined by the O-RU8's vendor and sufficient to accommodate the full software 16 
build. 17 
Note: procedures used in Software Management are covered by o-ran.software-management.yang module. 18 
A3.5.1 Software Package 19 
The software package is delivered by the O-RU8 vendor. 20 
Each software package includes: 21 
- manifest.xml 22 
- software files to be installed on O-RU8 23 
 24 
The name of package should follow the following format: 25 
“<Vendor Code><Vendor Specific Field>[#NUMBER].EXT” 26 
Where: 27 
- Vendor Code is a mandatory part which has two capital characters, 28 
- Vendor Specific Field  is any set of characters allo wed in filename. The value must not include character “_” 29 
(underscore) or “#” (hash). The value can be defined per vendor for the human readable information . Version 30 
information is necessary in the Vendor Specific Field which defines load version, 31 
- NUMBER is optional and used when the original file is split into smaller pieces –  number after “#” indicates the 32 
number of a piece. Numbering starts from 1 and must be continuous, 33 
- EXT is a mandatory part which defines the extension of filename. A vendor provides o ne or more  software 34 
packages. Each software package shall be compressed by zip. 35 
Note: the name of package needs a <Vendor Code> prefix to avoid issue if two vendors provide files with same name. 36 
Note: the NETCONF client shall support ZIP functionality to enable support of compressed files types.  37 
Note: the operator needs to manage and control which O -RU8 files will be stored and used in the file server, e.g., based 38 
on O-RU8 files provided by O-RU8 vendors and network configurations. The o perator needs to ma ke sure that only the 39 
expected version of O -RU8 files will be transferred from the file server to th e O-RU8. Different versions of files for O -40 
RU8 with the same vendor and same product code should be avoided. 41 

 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
117 
 
The content of the manifest.xml file allows to maintain software update process correctly in terms of compatibility 1 
between O-RU8 hardware and soft ware build to be downloaded. The content of the Manifest file prohibits the O -RU8 2 
from installing software builds designed for device based on different hardware. The format of the manifest.xml file is: 3 
<xml> 4 
<manifest version=”1.0”> /// @version describes version of file format (not the content) 5 
 <products> 6 
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”081820\.x11” name=”RUXX.x11” build-Id=”1”/>  7 
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”081820\.x12” name=”RUXX.x12” build-Id=”1”/> 8 
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”081818\…” name=”RUYY” build-Id=”2”/>  9 
  /// @vendor is as reported by O-RU8 10 
  /// @code is a regular expression that is checked against productCode reported by O-RU8 11 
  /// @name is optional and used for human reading – MUST NOT be used for other purposes! 12 
  /// @buildId is value of build@id (see below) 13 
 </products> 14 
 <builds> 15 
  <build id=”1” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 16 
  /// @id is index of available builds. 17 
  /// @bldName and @bldVersion are used in YANG (build-name, build-version) 18 
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 19 
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 20 
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 21 
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 22 
   /// @fileName and @fileVersion are used in YANG (name, version) 23 
   /// @path is full path (with name and extension) of a physical file, relative to 24 
package root folder,used in YANG (local-path) 25 
   /// @checksum is used to chech file integrity on O-RU8 side 26 
  </build> 27 
  <build id=”2” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 28 
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 29 
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 30 
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 31 
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 32 
   <file fileName=”zzzz” fileVersion=”1.5” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 33 
package -root-folder” checksum=”ABCDEF”/ > 34 
  </build> 35 
 </builds> 36 
</manifest> 37 
</xml> 38 
 39 
Note: Keywords in manifest.xml example are  in bold, the keywords must be strictly followed considering of cross -40 
vendor cases. 41 
Note 2: Correspondency between content of manifest.xml tags and content of o-ran-software-management.yang is: 42 
- XML tag "product vendor" corresponds to content leaf "vendor-code", 43 
- XML tag "code" corresponds to content of leaf "product-code", 44 
- XML tag "build-Id" corresponds to content of leaf "build-id", 45 
- XML tag "bldName" corresponds to content of leaf "build-name", 46 
- XML tag "bldVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "build-version", 47 
- XML tag "fileName" corresponds to content of leaf "name" in list "files",  48 
-XML tag "fileVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "version" in list "files"  49 
A3.5.2 Software Inventory 50 
Pre-condition:  51 
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 52 
Post-condition: 53 
- NETCONF client successfully collected the software inventory information from NETCONF server. 54 

 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
118 
 
 1 
 2 
Figure Annex 3-11: Inventory fetch call flow 3 
Software Inventory is fetched by a NETCONF Client using the NETCONF get  rpc filtered over the software -slot 4 
container. The response contains information about each software slot and its contents.  5 
The following information is provided by software-inventory reply message: 6 
a) name - name of the software slot (the name is defined by the O-RU8 vendor) 7 
b) status - status of the software package. Status of the package can be  8 
1.  - VALID - Slot contains a software build considered as proven valid. 9 
2.  - INVALID - software build is not currently  used by O -RU8. The software is considered by the O -RU8 as 10 
damaged (e.g. wrong CRC). 11 
3. Activation of a software slot containing an invalid software build shall be prohibited. Note: failed software 12 
install operation can cause a slot status to change to "Invalid". 13 
4.  - EMPTY - software slot does not contain a software package. Activation of an empty software slot shall be 14 
prohibited.  15 
c) active - indicates if the software stored in particular slot is activated at the moment. 16 
5.  - True - software slot contains an activ ated software build. Active::True can be assigned only for slots with 17 
status "Valid". At any time, only  one slot in the O -RU8 MUST be marked as Active::True. The O -RU8 shall 18 
reject activation for software slots with status "Empty" and "Invalid". 19 
6.  - False - software slot contains passive software build or is empty 20 
d) running - informs if software stored in particular slot is used at the moment. 21 
7.  - True - software slot contains the software build used by the O-RU8 in its current run. 22 
8.  - False - software slot contains a software build not used by O-RU8 at the moment. 23 
e) access – informs about access rights for the current slot 24 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
119 
 
- READ_ONLY – The slot is intended only for factory software, activation of such software slot means 1 
performing a factory reset operation and a return to factory defaults settings. 2 
- READ_WRITE – slot used for updating software 3 
f) product-code - product code provided by the vendor, specific to the product. 4 
g) vendor-code - unique code of the vendor. 5 
h) build-id - Identity associated with the software  build. This id is used to find the appropriate build -version for 6 
the product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 7 
i) build-name - Name of the software build. 8 
j) build-version - Version of the software build for the product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 9 
k) files – list of files in build 10 
l) name – name of one particular file 11 
m) version – version of the file 12 
n) local-path - complete path of the file on local file system 13 
o) integrity - result of the file integrity check 14 
- OK – file integrity is correct 15 
- NOK – file is coO-RU8pted 16 
If a slot contains a file with integrity::NOK, the O -RU8 shall mark the whole slot with status::INVALID. The content of 17 
a software-slot is fully under O -RU8's management - including removal of the content occupying the slot (in c ase the 18 
slot is subject of software update procedure), con trol of file system consistency and so on. The slot content shall not be 19 
removed until there is a need for new software to be installed.  20 
Note: The empty slot parameters shall be as follows 21 
name: up to vendor, not empty 22 
status: "INVALID" 23 
active: False 24 
running: False 25 
access: READ_WRITE 26 
product-code: up to vendor 27 
vendor code: up to vendor 28 
build-name: null (empty string) 29 
build-version: null (empty string) 30 
files: empty 31 
A3.5.3 Download 32 
Pre-condition:  33 
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 34 
Post-condition: 35 
- O-RU8 downloads all files specified and successfully stores the downloaded files in the O-RU8’s file system.  36

 1 
 2 
Figure Annex 3-12: Software download call flow 3 
Following types of authentications are supported for software-download: 4 
a) password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication  5 
b) certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 6 
The software-download rpc is used to trigger the downloading of software to the O -RU8. The download shall be 7 
performed using sFTP. The rpc specifies the URI of the remote location of the software files.  8 
The O-RU8 shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 9 
a) STARTED – software download operation has been started 10 
b) FAILED – software download operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error -message  11 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
121 
 
When the O -RU8 completes the software download or software download fails, t he O -RU8 shall send NETCONF 1 
download-event notification with one of the following statuses: 2 
a) COMPLETED 3 
b) AUTHENTICATION_ERROR -  source available, wrong credentials 4 
c) PROTOCOL_ERROR – sFTP protocol error 5 
d) FILE_NOT_FOUND -  source not available 6 
e) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason  7 
f) TIMEOUT -  source available, credentials OK, Operation timed out (e.g. source becomes unavailable during 8 
ongoing operation). 9 
The above will be repeated until all files which are required for the O -RU8 and which belong to the software package 10 
have been downloaded to the O-RU8. 11 
A3.5.4 Install 12

- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 14 
- At least one software slot with status active::False and running::False exists in O -RU8. 15 
- Software Download has been completed successfully and files are available in O-RU8 16 
Post-condition: 17 
- O-RU8 software is installed in the specified target software-slot. 18

Figure Annex 3-13: Software install call flow 3 
NETCONF software-install rpc is used  to install the previously downloaded software (all files provided in the 4 
package) to the specified target software-slot on O-RU8. This slot must have status active::False and running::False.  5 
The O-RU8 shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 6 
a) STARTED – software install operation has been started. 7 
b) FAILED – software install operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message. 8 
When O-RU8 completes the software install or software install procedure fails , the O-RU8 will send NETCONF install-9 
event notification with one of the following statuses: 10 
a) COMPLETED - Install procedure is successfully completed. 11 
b) FILE_ERROR – operation on the file resulted in in error, disk failure, not enough disk space, incompatible file 12 
format 13 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved

123 
 
c) INTEGRITY_ERROR – file is coO-RU8pted  1 
d) APPLICATION_ERROR – operation failed due to internal reason 2 
When the software install commences, the O -RU8 shall set the slot status to INVALID . A fter the install procedure 3 
finishes, the O-RU8 shall change the slot status to its  appropriate status. This operation avoid s reporting of inaccurate 4 
status when the install procedure is in operation or when it is inteO-RU8pted (e.g., by spurious reset operation). 5

- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 8 
- Software slot to be activated has status VALID. 9 
Post-condition: 10 
- O-RU8 software activates to the version of software-slot. 11

 1 
 2 
Figure Annex 3-14: Software activation call flow 3 
NETCONF software-activate rpc is used to activate the software. The name of the software-slot is specified in the 4 
activate request.  5 
The O-RU8 shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 6 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ

a) STARTED – software activation operation has been started 1 
b) FAILED – software activation operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message 2 
 3 
When the activation is completed, the O -RU8 shall send the NETCONF activation-event notification with the status of 4 
activation. The following status is returned in the NETCONF activation-event notifications. 5 
a) COMPLETED - Activation procedure is successfully completed. O -RU8 must be restarted via NETCONF reset  rpc 6 
for the new software to be activated. 7 
b) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason 8 
Only one software slot can be active at any time. Thus, successful software -activate command will set active::True to 9 
the slot that was provided in the rpc and automatically will set active::False to the previously active slot.  10 
NETCONF reset rpc shall be sent to O -RU8 to activate to the version of the sof tware-slot. O-RU8 restarts and performs 11 
startup procedure as described in Chapter 3 as regular startup with new software version running.  12 
A3.5.6 Software update scenario 13 
An example scenario of a successful software update procedure can be as follows: 14 
1. NETCONF cli ent performs a software inventory operation and determines that a new software package is 15 
available and can be installed on the O-RU8 16 
2. NETCONF client using the software -download rpc requests the O -RU8 to download a software package (if 17 
the software package contains several files, steps 2 -4 need to be performed repeatedly until all files have been 18 
downloaded) 19 
3. O-RU8 sends rpc response that download was started 20 
4. O-RU8 finishes downloading the file(s) and reports this by sending the download-event notification 21 
5. NETCONF client requests installation of the software using software -install rpc, and provides the slot name 22 
where the software needs to be installed along with a list of filenames to be in stalled (if the software package 23 
contains only one file, the list will contain only one entry) 24 
6. O-RU8 sends rpc response that installation was started 25 
7. O-RU8 sets installation slot status to INVALID 26 
8. O-RU8 installs the software and after successful installati on (with checksum control) changes status of the slot 27 
to VALID 28 
9. O-RU8 notifies the NETCONF client that the installation is finished using install- event notification 29 
10. NETCONF client requests the O-RU8 to activate the newly installed software using the software-activate rpc 30 
11. O-RU8 sends rpc response that activation was started 31 
12. For requested slot, O -RU8 changes active to True and at the same time sets activate to False on previously 32 
active slot 33 
13. O-RU8 notifies NETCONF client about activation finished using the activation-event notification 34 
14. NETCONF client restarts the O -RU8 forcing it to use the newly installed and activated software into use. O -35 
RU8 restarts as regular startup with new software version running. 36

O-RU8 can be reset to the factory default software by activating the software-slot containing the factory default software 1 
and initiating NETCONF reset  rpc. O -RU8 may clear persistent memory data during factory reset  as vendor 2 
implementation option. 3

A3.6 Configuration Management  5 
A3.6.1 Baseline configuration 6 
This chapter describes NETCONF standard operation (edit -config/get-config/get) [3] which belongs to the CM in 7 
Module to modify/retrieve any parameters in YANG modules . Examples below use o -ran-hardware as an example 8 
YANG module. 9 
Two following scenarios are feasible for Configuration Management purposes. 10 
- 2 phase (modify/commit) operation using writable running datastore 11 
- 3 phase (modify/commit/confirm) operation using candidate datastore. 12 
The 2-phase operation performs edit config on running datastore directly and confirm operation is not used. 13 
All O-RU8s shall support 2 phase operation, with 3 phase operations being optional. 14 
A3.6.1.1 Retrieve State 15 
O-RU8 Controller is able to retrieve state which is defined  in o -ran-hardware by using NETCONF <get -config> or 16 
<get> procedure: 17 
 18 
 19 
 Figure Annex 3-15: Retrieve Resource State 20

- O-RU8 Controller has completed exchange of NETCONF capabilities as part of connection establishment between O -22 
RU8 and O-RU8 Controllers. 23 
Post conditions: 24 
- O-RU8 controller has retrieved O-RU8 state as per <get-config> or <get> request.  25

O-RU8 Controller is able to change state which can be configurable by using NETCONF <edit -config> procedure 27 
without reset. 28

The availability state is derived from detected and active f aults and their impact to O -RU8’s operation. The availability 7 
state is not affected by faults caused by external reasons.  8 
• normal: There is no fault. 9 
• degraded: When major or critical fault a ffecting module or any of O -RU8’s subcomponents (e.g. transmitter) is 10 
active. 11 
• faulty: The critical fault affecting whole O-RU8 is active and O-RU8 can't continue any services. 12

A3.6.2 Framework for optional feature handling 17 
This section describes the common and optional features about Configuration Management.  18 
An O-RU8 may have some features which are not supported by other O -RU8s, i.e. optional feature (s). In this case, the 19 
O-RU8 needs to inform the  O-RU8 controller which features the O -RU8 can provide, and this can be achieved by 20 
exchanging NETCONF capabilities. 21 
Some of the YANG models are optional for the O -RU8 to support. For example, in this version of the management 22 
plane specification, those models associated with Externa l IO and Antenna Line Devices are not essential for the 23 
operation of the O-RAN fronthaul interface. Other mandatory models define optional feature capabilities.  24 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
132 
 
The NETCONF Server shall use the ietf -yang-library model (RFC 7895) [20] to list the namespace of the models 1 
supported by the Server. If an O -RU8/NETCONF server does not return the namespa ce associated with an optional 2 
YANG model, the NETCONF client determines that the O -RU8 does not support the optional capability associated with 3 
the model. 4 
In addition, for each supported schema, the ietf -yang-library lists the YANG feature names from this  module that a re 5 
supported by the server. The details of optional models and features are defined in Annex C. 6 
A3.6.3 M-Plane Operational State 7 
The o-ran-mplane-int YANG m odel allows the O-RU8 to report the connectivity to NETCONF clients on a per sub -8 
interface level. The client information includes the IP address(es) for the client(s) as well as the link -layer address used 9 
to forward packets towards the various management plane clients. 10 
A3.7 Performance Management 11 
This chapter provides the description of scenarios rela ted to performance management. It consists of 2 functions. One is 12 
for the measurement activation and the other is the collection of measurement results. 13 
A3.7.1  Measurement Activation and De-activation 14 
The measurement activation at the start-up installation is also allowed as described in chapter 3.  15 
Pre-condition:  16 
M-Plane is operational.  17 
Post-condition: 18 
Measurement is activated or deactivated as per NETCONF client’s request. 19 
This sub -section provides information about how to activate  and de -activate the perform ance measurement via 20 
NETCONF <edit-config> to O-RU8. The performance measurement is defined as o -ran-performance-management-cpri 21 
YANG module. In case of multiple NETCONF clients, only one NETCONF client shall  activate/deactivate the 22 
measurements in the O-RU8. 23 
In the performance-management YANG module, the following parameters are defined. 24 
- group of the measurement results, e.g., transceiver- measurement-result and, rx-window-measurement-25 
object. 26 
- measurement-interval: measurement interval for the measurement-objects to measure the performance 27 
periodically, e.g., 300, 600, 900 seconds. It is defined per the group of the measurement result. 28 
- measurement-object: target metric to measure the performance, e.g., RX_POWER, TX_POWER, defined  as 29 
key parameter. 30 
- active: enable/disable the performance measurement per measurement-object. This value is Boolean. Default is 31 
FALSE. 32 
- start-time and end-time: to report the time of measurement start and end for the measurement-object at each 33 
measurement-interval. 34 
- object-unit: unit to measure the performance per object, e.g., O-RU8, physical port number, antenna, carrier. The 35 
object-unit may be configurable Identifier object-unit-id means e.g., physical port number when object unit set 36 
to physical port number. 37 
- report-info: the reporting info to the measurement-object, e.g., MAXIMUM , MINIMUM, FIRST, LATEST , 38 
FREQUENCY_TABLE and COUNT. Multiple info can be considered for one object if necessary. 39 
- Optional configurable parameter(s) for report -info: some configurable parameters to report, e.g., function, bin-40 
count, upper-bound, lower-bound. For the bin- count configuration, it shall be les s than the parameter max-41 
bin-count that is the capability information of NETCONF server for the maximum configurable value for bin -42 
count. 43 

 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
133 
 
- Additional reporting information for report-info: some additional information to report info, e.g., date-and-time. 1 
 2 
The detail of the parameters per measurement-object and the group of measurement result are defined in Annex B. 3 
The measurement-interval of measurement-object may be set to common or different  values per group of the 4 
measurement result.  5 
It is allowed that the measurement is activated and deactivated at any  time. When different parameter measurements 6 
have intervals with a common factor, the O -RU8 shall synchronize the boundary of these measurements aligned with 7 
this factor, irrespective of when the different measurements are activated. And all of start points of the measurement-8 
intervals shall be synchronized to zero o’clock mid- night by using an equation {full seconds (hour, minute and second) 9 
modulo ‘ measurement-interval’ = 0}, in order to ensure the same start and end of the measurement-intervals 10 
between O-RU8s. For more detail see the following illustration. 11 
 12 
Figure Annex 3-25: synchronization of measurement-interval. 13 
 14 
The modification of the configurable parameters for the measurement shall be allowed  while active for the 15 
corresponding measurement-object is set to FALSE. 16 
All of the measurements are optionally supported in the O-RU8.  17 
The report-info, e.g., count, shall be started from 0 at the boundary of every measurement-interval. No accumulation 18 
is applied between the measurement-intervals. 19 
A3.7.2   Collection and Reporting of Measurement Result 20 
This sub-section provides the description of scenarios used to collect measurement results. There are two options. 21 
- NETCONF process: Create -subscription from NETCONF client and NETCONF notification from NETC ONF 22 
server are used.  23 
- File Management process: File upload mechanism is used for the  measurement file from O -RU8 to configured file 24 
server(s) that O-RU8 can reach to. 25 
Both methods are mandatory for the O-RU8. The method(s) to be used is the matter of NETCONF client. 26 
In case of multiple NETCONF clients, the O -RU8 shall report the  same notification-based measurement results to all 27 
subscribed NETCONF clients, and the O-RU8 shall upload file-based results to all configured fileservers. 28 
A3.7.2.1 NETCONF process 29

This process needs the NETCONF capability: urn:ietf:params:netconf:capability:notification:1.0  1 
1. NETCONF client subscribes to one or more measurement  group(s) and/or measurement-object(s) to collect the 2 
measurement result by sending NETCONF < subscribe-notification> to NETCONF server in the O -RU8. In this 3 
message, startTime and stopTime for the notification may be configurable. NETCONF client can con figure the 4 
notification-interval in the performance-measurement YANG module.  5 
2.  NETCONF server sends NETCONF notif ication messages periodically to the client as con figured by  the 6 
notification-interval. The NETCONF notification message contains subscribed measurement group(s) and/or 7 
measurement-object(s). The notification-interval doesn’t need to be same as the measurement-interval. The 8 
notification timing different from the measurement-interval is a matter to O-RU8 implementation. 9

When notification-interval is larger than measurement-interval, one notification may contain multiple stats which 3 
have consecutive periods indicating start-time and end-time for the measurement. 4 
When notification-interval is smaller than measurement-interval, one notification may not contain the stats which 5

For example, when notification -interval = 60min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 7 
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains 2 measurement  results for 8 
measurement-object#A with  consecutive start-time and end-time, and 4 measurement results for measurement-9 
object#B with consecutive start-time and end-time.  10

30min and measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains one measurement 12 
results for measurement -object#B but not for measurement-object#A. next notification contains both measurements 13 
result for measurement-object#A and #B. 14

A3.7.2.2 File Management process 16 
NETCONF client needs to con figure a parameter of performance measurement YANG module ‘enable-SFTP-upload’ 17 
to enable or disable the periodic file upload mechanism via NETCONF <edit-config>. Its default is FALSE. 18 
In addition, the performance measur ement YANG module defines file-upload-interval, remote-SFTP-upload-path, 19 
credentials information of the file server and enable-random-file-upload as configurable parameters. 20 
Following types of authentications are supported for performance file upload: 21 
a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication  22 
b) Certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 23 
When the parameter enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE, O -RU8 shall store the performance measurement files in the 24 
generic folder in O -RU8, i.e., O -RAN/PM/. Every file-upload-interval, O-RU8 pushes the latest file to upload to the  25 
remote-SFTP-upload-path of the con figured SFTP servers if enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE. Otherwise, the 26 
performance measurement file is not created and uploaded. T he number of maximum performance files to be stored in 27 
O-RU8 simultaneously is a matter for O -RU8 implementation. The O -RU8 shall manage its own storage space by 28 
deleting the older files autonomously.  29 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
136 
 
The O-RU8 shall ensure that the start -time and the end-time within the name of the performance measurement file are 1 
synchronized with the same manner as measurement-interval by using file-upload-interval. 2 
If the parameter enable-random-file-upload is set to TRUE, the O-RU8 shall randomize the timing to upload SFTP file 3 
after the performance measurement file is ready to upload. The randomized timing is an  O-RU8 implementation matter 4 
and shall not be later than next file-upload-interval. 5 
The file name of the performance measurement is: 6 
9. C<start-time>_<end-time>_<name>.csv 7 
- Starting with a capital letter “C”. 8 
- Format of <start-time> and <end-time> can be local time or UTC. 9 
10. Local time format is YYYYMMDDHHMM+HHMM, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute, timezone “+” or 10 
“-“, hour and minute for the time zone. 11 
11. UTC format is YYYYMMDDHHMMZ, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute and with a special UTC 12 
designator ("Z")   13 
12. Time zone offset is provided by timezone-utc-offset in o-ran-operation.yang. 14 
- <name> in ietf-hardware is used  15 
- “_” underscore is located between <start-time>, <end-time> and <name> 16 
- File extension is “csv” as csv format file. 17 
Example of measurement file is: 18 
C201805181300+0900_201805181330+0900_ABC0123456.csv. 19 
 20 
The file format of the performance measurement has following rule: 21 
1. Each line starts with the measurement-object identifier, which measurement can be switched to TRUE or FALSE 22 
by active parameter. The identifier of each measurement-object is defined in Annex B. 23 
2. After the measurement-object identifier, the name of measurement-object, start-time, end-time are followed. 24 
3. Since the report-info results of any measurement-object are measured per object-unit, object-unit-id and set of 25 
report-info are repeated in one line. 26 
4. When multiple report-info parameters exist per object-unit, all of the report-info are consecutively listed until the 27 
next object-unit-id. The order of parameters, such as object -unit-id, report-info and additional information for the 28 
report-info, shall be same as the order of those listed in NETCONF notification defined in o- ran-performance-29 
management-cpri YANG module. 30 
Example of measurement result in one line is: 31 
1, RX_ON_TIME, 2018-05-18T13:00:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00, 0, 123, AAAA, 1, 123, BBBB, 2, 123, CCCC, 3, 32 
123, DDDD 33

- end-time: 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00 as measurement end-time 37 
- EAXC_ID: 0 38

A3.8 Fault Management 34 
Fault management is responsible f or sending alarm notifications to the NETCONF Client. FM contains Fault 35 
Management Managed Element and via this Managed Element alarm notifications can be disabled or enabled.  36 
The NETCONF Server is responsible for managing an “active-alarm-list”. Alarms with severity “warning” are excluded 37 
from this list. When an alarm is detected it is added to the list; when the alarm reason disappears then the alarm is 38 
cleared - removed from the “active -alarm-list”. Furthermore, when the elemen t that was the “fault -source” of an alarm 39 
is deleted then all related alarms are removed from the “active-alarm-list”. 40 
The NETCONF Client can read “active-alarm-list” by get rpc operation. 41 

 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
138 
 
 1 
Figure Annex 3-28: Read Active Alarms 2 
A3.8.1 Alarm Notification 3 
The NETCONF Server is responsible to send <alarm -notif> to a NETCONF Client when the NETCONF Client has 4 
“subscribed” to alarm notification and: 5 
- a new alarm is detected (this can be the same alarm as an already existing one, but reported against a different 6 
“fault-source” than the existing alarm)  7 
- an alarm is removed from the list   8 
Removal of alarms from the list due to deletion of  “fault-source” element is considered as clearing and cause sending of 9 
<alarm-notif> to the NETCONF Client. This applies to alarms which were explicitly related to the deleted “fault -10 
source” element. The r ationale for such is to avoid misalignment between NETCONF Clients when one NETCONF 11 
Client deletes an element.  12 
NETCONF Server reports in <alarm-notif> only for new active or cancelled alarms, not all active alarms. 13 
 14 
Figure Annex 3-29: Alarm Notification 15

A3.8.3 Fault Sources 3 
Alarm notifications reported by NETCONF Server contain element “fault -source” which indicates the origin of an 4 
alarm. In general values of “fault-source” are based on names defined as YANG leafs: 5 
- Source (Examples: fan, module, PA, port) 6 
13. indicates that origin of the alarm within the O-RU8. Value of “fault-source” is based on element name. 7 
Note: In case the NETCONF Server re ports an unknown “fault-source”, the NETCONF Client can discard the 8 
<alarm-notif>. 9 
- Source (other than when an element is within the O-RU8) 10 
Value of fault-source may be empty or may identify the most likely external candidate; for example, antenna line.   11 
14.  12 
Alarms with different “fault-id”, “fault-source” or "fault-severity" are independent: 13 
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-id” may be reported with different “fault-source”.  14 
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-source” may be reported with different “fault-id”.  15 
- When an alarm with a "fault -id" and a "fault -source" is reported with a "fault -severity" and its severity of alarm 16 
condition is upgraded or degraded, NETCONF server reports a new alarm with the same "fault -id" and the same 17 
"fault-source" with the upgraded or degraded "fault -severity" with "is -cleared"::FALSE and clears the previous 18 
alarm with the report of the "fault-id", "fault-source" and "fault-severity" with "is-cleared":: TRUE.  19 
The range of "fault-id" is separated to common and vendor specific. The common fault -ids are defined in Annex A and 20 
more number will be used in future. The vendor specific range for the fault-id shall be [1000 .. 65535]. 21 
Alarm notifications reported by the NETCONF Server contain names of the “affected-objects” which indicate elements  22 
affected by the fault. In case the origin of the alarm is within  the O-RU8, other elements than “fault -source” which will 23 
not work correctly due to the alarm are reported via “affected -objects”. In case the origin of the fault is outside of the O-24 
RU8, the O-RU8 elements which will not work correctly due to the fault are reported via “affected-objects”. 25

A3.9.1 File System Structure 15 
The file System structure of the O -RU8 is represented as a logical structure that is used by the file management 16 
procedures defined in the rest of this chapter.  If the O-RU8’s physical file structure differs from the logical file structure 17 
defined below, the O-RU8 is responsible for performing the mapping between the two structures. 18 
The O-RU8 shall support the standardized logical folders. In this version of the M -Plane specification, the following 19 
standardized folders are defined: 20 
O-RAN/log/ 21 
O-RAN/PM/ 22 
O-RAN/transceiver/ 23 
The O-RU8 may additionally support vendor defined folders which are out of scope of this specification.  24 
A3.9.2 File Management Operation: upload 25

file can be uploaded by one upload operation. The O-DU8/NMS triggers file upload operation to O-RU8. 27 
Simultaneous multiple file upload operations can b e supported under the same sFTP connection between O -RU8 to O-28 
DU8/NMS. If the O-RU8 has the number of limitation to upload simultaneously as a capability, it is allowed that O -RU8 29 
reports failure notification for the upload request which is larger than the  capability. The behavio ur of O -DU8/NMS is 30 
out of scope when O-DU8/NMS receives failure notification from the O-RU8. 31 
Following rpc is used for upload operation. 32 
-rpc: file-upload 33 
-  input 34 
-  local-logical-file-path: the logical path of file to be uploaded (no wildcard is allowed) 35 
-  remote-file-path: URI of file on the O-DU8/NMS 36 
-  output 37

A3.10 Synchronization Aspects 10 
This chapter provides the Management Plane’s interactions with various aspects of the time synchronization of the O-11 
RU8. In general, the O-RU8 is responsible for managing its synchronization status, to select one or more synchronization 12 
input source(s) (based on vendor specific implementation) and assure that the resulting accuracy meets that required by 13 
the Radio Access Technology being implemented. 14 
A3.10.1 Sync Status Object 15 
This sync container provides synchronization state of the module. If the O -DU8 is interested in Sync status, it may send 16 
NETCONF <subscribe-notification> to the NETCONF Server in the O-RU8.  Event notifications will be sent whene ver 17 
the state of the O-RU8 synchronization changes. 18 
The State of O-RU8 synchronization is indicated by the following allowed values: 19

146 
 
- LOCKED: O-RU8 is in the synchronisation status.  1 
- UNLOCKED: O-RU8 is not  in synchronisation status.  2 
A3.10.2 CPRI Configuration 3 
Rate 4 
CPRI line bit rate 10137.6 Mbit/s(64B/66B line coding), 24330.24 Mbit/s(64B/66B line coding) 5 
 6 
Ethernet pointer 7 
The preferred value is used by the core in negotiating a common rate with its peer. The value  must be between 20 8 
and 63 decimal, where 20 i s the highest bandwidth, or 0 to indicate no Ethernet channel. To ensure correct 9 
operation it should be set before link initialization. 10 
A3.10.3 CPRI Synchronization Status 11 
Those parameters indicate the CPRI synchronization status.  12 
Standby: Waiting to be configured to start up CPRI. No transmission or reception of CPRI.  13 
L1 Synchronization: The line bit rate of the interface is determined and both master and slave ports reach   layer 14 
1synchronization up to state HFNSYNC. 15 
 Protocol version setup: During this state, a common protocol version of CPRI is determined.  16 
C&M plane setup: A common C&M channel bit rate is determined. 17 
Negotiation: Application in master and slave ports negotiate the CPRI usage  18 
Link up: The link has been established and the frequency has been synchronized 19

A3.11 Operations Use Cases 1 
A3.11.1 Supervision Failure 2 
Section 3.6 describes the procedure by which an O -RU8 uses the expiry of a supervision watchdog timer to trigger 3 
“supervision failure” condition. 4 
Note, an O -RU8 operating in supervision failure may st ill have NETCONF sessions established with one or more 5 
NETCONF clients with non-“sudo” privileges.  6 
An O -RU8 that detects a supervision failure shall immediately cease RF transmission. The O -RU8 shall perform an 7 
autonomous recovery reset procedure. This pr ocedure will trigger the re -initialization of the transport layer and re -8 
commencement of the start-up installation procedures defined in section 3. 9 
A3.11.2 Log management 10 
There are two type of log managements, troubleshooting log and trace log. They are independen t each other. 11 
Troubleshooting log file contains the logs continuously collected before <start -troubleshooting-logs> rpc. Any logs 12 
collected after <start-troubleshooting-logs> rpc are not contained. 13 
Trace log file contains the logs continuously collected af ter <start -trace-logs> rpc. Any logs collected before <start -14 
trace-logs> rpc are not contained. 15 
A3.11.2.1 Troubleshooting 16 
By requesting technical logs an O -RU8 controller is able to get  collected log  data files that can be used for 17 
troubleshooting purposes.  18 
The O -RU8 provides all possible  troubleshooting log  files. The contents and log formats are dependent on O -RU8 19 
implementation. 20 
The number and size of files provided by O-RU8 is not restricted but the O -RU8 may keep the number and size of files 21 
reasonably small to allow completion of the whole “Troubleshooting data upload” scenario (all files) within 15 minutes  22 
(with target to complete within 3 minutes). It is also recommended to provide more useful files first.  23 
Note, the O -RU8 controller is free to continue the s cenario till completion past the allowed tim e or skip requesting 24 
further files. 25 
The files should be compressed with compression method indicated by file name extension:  26 
• .gz (DEFLATE),  27 
• .lz4 (LZ4),  28 
• .xz (LZMA2 - xz utils),  29 
• .zip (DEFLATE - zlib library). 30 
O-RU8 shall start collecting the troubleshooting logs.  31 
The rpc <start -troubleshooting-logs> triggers the O -RU8 to start creating files containing troubleshooting logs. 32 
Completed generation of files is indicated by NETCONF server to NETCONF client in form of a notification. 33

A3.11.2.2 Trace 3 
By requesting trace logs an O-RU8 controller is able to get collected log data files that can be used for trace purposes.  4 
The O-RU8 provides all possible trace log files. The contents and log formats are dependent on O -RU8 implementation. 5 
The files should be compressed with compression method indicated by file name extension. 6 
O-RU8 shall start collecting the trace logs at the mo ment of receiving <start -trace-logs> rpc. Notification <trace -log-7 
generated> shall be periodically send to O -RU8 controller once collected logs stored in file(s) is(are) ready. URL of 8 
newly created log file(s) shall be included in notification. The number and size of files provided by O -RU8 in a single 9 
<trace-log-generated> notification is not restricted but the O -RU8 may keep the number and size of files reasonably  10 
small to allow completion of the whole “Trace data upload” scenario (all files from notifica tion) within 15 minutes 11 
(with target to complete within 3 minutes). 12 
Note: Timing of creating trace log files is up to O-RU8 implementation. 13 
After <stop-trace-logs> rpc received from controller, O -RU8 is mandated to stop collecting trace logs and to send la st 14 
<trace-log-generated> notification with the is -notification-last:: TRUE and URL(s) of file(s) which contain log data 15 
collected between previous <trace-log-generated> notification and <stop-trace-logs> rpc.  16 
The file transfer mechanism for the created tr ace log files shall be handled by the file management described in Chapter 17 
9 File Management. 18

A3.11.3 Operational aspects of Antenna Line Devices 4 
An O-RU8 can connect to one or more external equipment such as a RET, MultiRET, MHA, RAE and etc. 5 
For the communication with the external equipment, AISG 2.0 protocol [26] as Layer 7 application and HDLC protocol 6 
as Layer 2 data link are used. 7 
- HDLC protocol is standardized by ISO/IEC 13239 ( https://www.iso.org/standard/37010.html). Detailed information 8 
can also be found in TS 25.462 [27]. 9 
- AISG 2.0 protocol is standardized by “Control interface for antenna lin e devices Standard No. AISG v2.0” [26] 10 
which is an adaptation of Iuant interface application layer defined in TS 25.466 [28]  and formerly in TS 25.463 [29].  11 
An O-RU8 may provide one or more ALD ports supporting connection with Antenna Line Devices. Each A LD port 12 
shall be able to support more than one ALD (i.e., a chained ALD configuration).  13 


 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
152 
 
This section describes the communication mechanisms based on AISG 2.0 protocol  [26]. For communication with 1 
external equipment, AISG 2.0 uses Application Part protocols  (RETAP, TMAAP etc.) at Layer 7 and  HDLC as a Layer 2 
2 datalink protocol. 3 
Note, further definitions of O -RU8 support for Antenna Line Devices will be included in a future version of this 4 
specification, and will target support of the AISG 3.0 protocol. 5 
A3.11.3.1 HDLC Interworking 6 
HDLC protocol is standardized by ISO/IEC 13239. Detailed information can also be found in TS 2 5.462 [27]. The 7 
AISG 2.0 protocol is standardized by “Control interface for antenna line devices Standard No. AISG v2.0” which is an 8 
adaptation of Iuant interface application layer defined in TS 25.466 [28] and formerly in TS 25.463 [29]. 9 
Note: the assumed HDLC communication speed is 9600 bits per second. 10 
In order to handle collision detection in the HDLC branch, an O-RU8 supporting the ALD functionality shall support the 11 
following running counters reported using the corresponding YANG model:  12 
-  Frames with wrong FCS 13 
-  Frames without stop flag 14 
-  Number of received octets 15 
For running counters served by the O -RU8, both the O -RU8 and NETCONF Client shall handle wrap-over mechanism 16 
in a way, that wrap over zero is not considered as erroneous situation. 17 
A NETCONF client can recover these counters. From the changes observed in above counters, a NETCONF Client can 18 
deduce the presence of a collision on the HDL C bus. Additional diagnostic information may be derived from how these 19 
counters are incrementing. 20 
Additionally, the O-RU8 implements "RPC Status" to indicate status of last "ald-communication" RPC to requestor. 21 
-  Status - flow control indicator of last requested operation (Status of RPC). 22 
Prior to any communication with ALD(s), the O -RU8 shall provide ALDs wit h DC power. The way of how DC power 23 
is managed is out of scope of this interface specification. 24 
In order to support collision detection and flow cont rol, the following reference architecture with functional split is 25 
defined: 26

A3.11.3.2 ALD Operations 4 
The NETCONF Client sends RPC <ald-communication> to the O-RU8. The RPC has following input parameters: 5 
- leaf: ald-port-id (uint8) - contains the identity of the ALD port. The O -RU8 shall output the data to (corresponds to 6 
O-RU8 resources provided to NETCONF Client as inventory information) 7 
- leaf: ald-req-msg (up to 1 200 bytes) - may contain HDLC address, control bits and payload (see: TS 25.462 for 8 
details) 9 
The O-RU8 performs HDLC communication with the ALD as follows: immediately after the requested payload is sent  10 
to the ALD over the desired ALD port, the O-RU8 switches the ALD port into reception mode.  11 
Note, for details of HDLC transmission and reception algorithm, please see TS 25.462, chapter 4.5 "Message timing". 12 
Bits received within reception window are formed to octets and inserted as payload into ald -resp-msg. 13 
The O-RU8 responds to the NETCONF Client using the <rpc-reply> message containing following parameters: 14 
- leaf: ald-port-id (uint8) 15 
- leaf: status 16 
- leaf: ald-resp-msg (up to 1200 bytes) 17 
- leaf: frames-with-wrong-crc (4 bytes) 18 
- leaf: frames-without-stop-flag (4 bytes) 19 
- leaf: number-of-received-octets (4 bytes) 20 
Note: In case there is no response from the ALD received within the reception window, the record " ald-resp-msg" in 21 
<rpc-reply> sent by the O-RU8 shall be empty. 22 
After reception, the O -RU8 shall wait an additional 3ms before the next transmission towards HDLC bus is initiated. 23 
See TS 25.462, chapter 4.5 "Message timing" for details. 24 
 25 

 ORAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00 
 
© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
154

Figure Annex 3-42: ALD Message Transfer 2 
General scenario 3 
Precondition:  4 
M-Plane connectivity between NETCONF Client and NETCONF Server is successfully established. NETCONF Server 5 
reports presence of the supported HDLC Primary Devices. 6 
 7 
1) NETCONF Client triggers DC voltage on  desired ALD ports using NETCONF <edit -config> RPC. After DC is 8 
turned on - NETCONF Client waits 3s. 9 
2) NETCONF Client performs HDLC link speed alignment to assure that all ALDs connected to a particular port have 10 
switched themselves to the correct baud rate used by this port.  11 
3) NETCONF Client performs HDLC bus scan using desired HDLC Primary Device offered by O -RU8. 12 
3) NETCONF Client determines presence of HDLC Secondary Devices. 13 
4) NETCONF Client assigns HDLC addresses to desired HDLC Secondary Devices.  14 
5) NETCONF Client initiates HDLC layer for secondary devices by sending SNRM command.  15 
6) NETCONF Client starts polling procedure for every HDLC-addressed Secondary Device. 16

A3.11.4 Operational aspects of external IO 4 
An O-RU8 can connect to one or more input and output ports for external device supervision and control. 5 
The External IO has the following functions 6 
- INPUT: Supervising external devices 7 
- OUTPUT: Controlling external devices 8 
Also external IO function include signalling to get the O-RU8 and O-RU8 controller in sync, enables port monitoring on 9 
the O-RU8 and provide s notification from the O-RU8 to an O -RU8 controller, and provides control from an O -RU8 10 
controller to the O-RU8 and enables output port controlling on the O-RU8.  11 
The O-RU8 only implements external IO yang module if the O-RU8 supports External IO aspect. 12 
A change in condition of the external IO shall not affect other O -RU8 services such as RF transmission  / reception 13 
behaviour. 14 
A3.11.4.1 External input 15 
This section explains single external input line case. For multiple external inputs case, same behaviour for each input 16 
shall be processed individually. 17 
For input, the O-RU8 and O-RU8 controller shall support two scenarios.  18 
[1] To retrieve input state from O-RU8 controller and respond the input state from the O-RU8 to O-RU8 controller. 19 
[2] To send notification from the O-RU8 to O-RU8 controller when input state is changed. 20 
The value shall be 21 
 TRUE: Circuit is open. 22 
 FALSE: Circuit is closed 23 
When nothing is connected to the line the value shall be TRUE. 24

[1] To retrieve output state from O-RU8 controller and respond the output state from the O-RU8 to O-RU8 controller.  7

 retrieve sync-state – the synchronization state of the O-RU8 4 
The detail of O-RU8 information, please see corresponding YANG modules in Annex D.  5 
A3.12.2 User plane message routing 6 
The purpose of U-Plane configuration is to define the relationship between U -Plane application endpoints in the O-DU8 7 
and those in the O-RU8.  8 
Precondition: 9 
• M-Plane connectivity is established between NETCONF Client and NETCONF Server 10 
A3.12.2.1 Configurable format for AxC_ID  11 
The AxC_ID is used by C/U -plane application to manage CPRI communication between desired C/U -Plane application 12 
components in O-DU8 and O-RU8. 13 
Similar as  eAxC_ID defined in [2], the AxC_ID consists of four parameters: DU -PORT, RU -PORT, CC- ID and 14 
BAND-SECTOR-ID. Order of parameters in AxC_ID must follow definitions in CPRI  spec. In this version, the length 15 
of AxC_ID is constant and equal to 16 bits. The assignment of AxC_ID bits to parameters is not fixed.  16 
DU_Port_ID is u sed to differentiate processing units at O-DU8, with default 0.  BAND-SECTOR-ID is used for 17 
aggregated cell identifier, with default 0. 18 
CC_ID is used to distinguish Carrier Components, with default 0.  RU_Port_ID is used to differentiate spatial streams 19 
or beams on the O-RU8, with default 0. 20 
Bit assignment usage where 4  bits are assigned to the BAND -SECTOR-ID, 4 bits for CC -ID, 4 bit for DU- PORT-ID 21 
and 4 bits for RU-PORT-ID is shown below: 22 
<du-port-bitmask> 1111000000000000 </du-port-bitmask> 23 
           <band-sector-bitmask> 0000111100000000 </band-sector-24 
bitmask> 25 
<ccid-bitmask> 0000000011110000 </ccid-bitmask> 26 
<ru-port-bitmask> 0000000000001111 </ru-port-bitmask> 27 
The low-level-rx-endpoints a nd low -level-tx-endpoints i nclude axcid, and  also CPRI IQ bit mapping related 28 
information will be included in low -level-rx-endpoints and low -level-tx-endpoints defined in o -ran-uplane-conf-29 
cpri.yang. 30 
A3.12.2.2 AxC information transfer 31 
The 16 bit AxC ID information needs to be transferred from  O-DU8 to O-RU8. And the information can be transferred 32 
via vendor specific BYTEs as defined in CPRI specification,  as below figure. Z.16.x,Z.80.x,  Z.144.x,  Z.208.x and etc 33 
control words can be used to transfer the O-DU8 to O-RU8.  34

A3.12.2.3 U-Plane endpoint addressing 7 
Parameter “axc-id” for low-level-tx-endpoint and low-level-rx-endpoint, defined using an unsigned 16 bit integer, shall 8 
follow the AxC_ID addressing schema defined in section 12.2.1.  9 
The NETCONF Client is responsible for assigning unique values to "axc_id" addresses of all low -level-rx-endpoint 10 
elements and low -level-tx-endpoint elements, that are linked to the same interface element and are referenced by low -11
