© 2020 O-RAN Alliance  All Rights Reserved 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ  
161 
 
level-rx-link or/ low -level-tx-link respectively. Note: The same AxC_id can be assigned to low -level-rx-endpoint and 1 
low-level-tx-endpoint. 2 
The NETCONF Server shall reject configuration requests violating the above -mentioned rules. 3 
The default value of the "axc-id" parameters is zero. 4 
A3.12.2.4 General configuration scenario 5 
Below is described the general scenario to be followed by a NETCONF Client in order to properly configure  6 
communication between C/U-Plane endpoints in the O-DU8 and O-RU8. 7 
All operations can be performed in any order (including combining some of them in one request) provided assumed 8 
result (overall configuration) of each request sent by NETCONF Client is valid. Note selected highlighted rules below:  9 
-  axc -id is u nique for all endpoints linked wi th same interface element and linked with any low -level-rx-link or low-10 
level-tx-link element 11 
-  at the moment of creation, every low -level-rx-link must be linked to an existing rx -array-carrier element and existing 12 
processing-element element  13 
-  at the mom ent of creation, every low -level-tx-link must be linked to an existing t x-array-carrier element and existing 14 
processing-element element 15 
1) NETCONF Client determines the presence of following elements offered by NETCONF Serv er: 16 
- tx-arrays  - by fetching the list of tx-arrays in o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri.yang 17 
- rx-arrays - by fetching the list of rx-arrays in o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri.yang 18 
- low-level-tx-endpoint elements - by fetching the list static-low-level-tx-endpoints in o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri.yang 19 
- low-level-rx-endpoint elements - by fetching the list static-low-level-rx-endpoints in o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri.yang 20 
- interface elements - by fetching list of interfaces in o-ran-interfaces-cpri.yang 21 
2) NETCONF Client determines ca pabilities exposed by static -low-level-tx-and points and static -low-level-rx-22 
endpoints. Additionally. NETCONF Client determines capabilities exposed by "endpoint- types" and "endpoint -23 
capacity-sharing-groups" and specific parameters proprietary to [tr]x- array(s). Obtained information must be respected 24 
when NETCONF Client con figures low -level-[tr]x-endpoints refferenced to static- low-level[tr]x-endpoints by 25 
parameter "name". 26 
3) For elements determined in step 1) NETCONF Client examines relationship between  27 
- static-low-level-tx-endpoint elements and tx-array elements in o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri.yang 28 
- static-low-level-rx-endpoint elements and rx-array elements in o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri.yang 29 
- static-low-level-tx-endpoint elements and interface elements 30 
- static-low-level-rx-endpoint elements and interface elements 31 
- tx-arrays, rx-arrays and their elements in o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri.yang. 32 
4) NETCONF Client may optionally perform “Transport connectivity checking procedure” to NETCONF Server, as 33 
described in section 4.6.  34 
Note: After this step is successfully completed, a NETCONF Client knows which low -level-tx-endpoint elements and 35 
low-level-rx-endpoint elements offered by the NETCONF Server are accessible for TX/RX endpoints served by the 36 
NETCONF Client. 37 
5) NETCONF Client determines accessible low -level-rx-endpoint elements and low -level-tx-endpoint elements, that 38 
are suitable for the desired cell configuration (i.e. are linked with specific antenna arrays and are able to support desired 39 
type of traffic). 40 
6 ) NETCONF Client assigns unique values to the axc-id(s) to the endpoints determined in step 1. 41

Note: uniqueness of axc-id is mandatory within all endpoints related to same interface elements and having relationship 1

7) NETCONF Client creates tx-array-carrier(s) and rx-array-carrier(s) 3

A3.12.3.1 Carrier creation  16 
This section provides basic scenario for carrier creation procedure. Precondition for  below steps is to fulfil steps f rom 17 
subsection 12.2.3 18 
1) NETCONF Client creates the tx-array-carriers in relation to the desired tx -arrays. Note that generally number of 19 
tx-array-carriers will be the same as multiple of the desired number of tx -arrays and the number of component 20 
carriers. 21 
2) NETCONF Client creates the  rx-array-carriers in relation to the desired  rx-arrays. Note that generally number of 22 
rx-array-carriers will be the same as multiple of the desired number of rx -arrays and the number of compo nent 23 
carriers. 24 
3) NETCONF Client creates the processing-elements related to interfaces offering access to endpoints. 25 
4) NETCONF Client creates the low -level-tx-links containing relationship to the existing tx -array-carriers, low-26 
level-tx-endpoints and existing processing-elements. 27 
5) NETCONF Client creates the  low-level-rx-links containing the relationship to existing  rx-array-carriers, low-28 
level-rx-endpoints and existing processing-elements. 29

A3.12.3.2 12.3.2 Activation, deactivation and sleep 3 
The NETCONF Client performs activation by setting the value of the parameter “active” at tx -array-carrier element / 4 
rx-array-carrier element to “ACTIVE”. 5 
The NETCONF Client performs deactivation by setting the value of the parameter “active” at t x-array-carrier element / 6 
rx-array-carrier element to “INACTIVE” 7 
Communication between rel ated U-Plane endpoints is enabled under condition, that for corre sponding tx-array-carrier 8 
or rx-array-carrier value of parameter “active” is “ACTIVE” and value of parameter “state” is “READY”. Otherwise 9 
communication is disabled. 10 
The NETCONF Client can pu t the tx -array-carrier / rx-array-carrier to sleep by setting value of parameter “active” in 11 
the corresponding tx-array-carrier element / rx-array-carrier element to “SLEEP”. 12 
A particular t x-array-carrier / rx-array-carrier is in sleep mode when value of i ts parameter “active” is “SLEEP” and 13 
value of its parameter “state” is “READY”. 14 
Below diagram shows possible transitions to be followed by "active" and "state". 15

Annex 4 Alarm definition 1 
This section contains example alarms which may be reported. 2 
Obviously, alarms that are not applicable in given H W design or SW configuration shall not be reported. For example, 3 
alarms related to fan monitoring are applicable to HW variants with fans. 4 
In many cases alar m detection method is HW specific. It is assumed that alarm detection method is reliable to avoid 5 
undetected alarms and false alarms. It is also expected that the NETCONF Server is applying mechanisms to avoid 6 
unreasonably fast toggling of alarms’ state. 7 
 8 
The example alarms table has following columns: 9 
Fault id – Numerical identifier of alarm. This ID shall be used in <alarm-notif> message (fault-id parameter). 10 
Name – Name of the alarm. 11 
Meaning – Description of alarm, describes high level meaning of the alarm. 12 
Start condition –  Defines conditions which must be fulfilled to generate alarm. If filtering ti me is needed, then it must 13 
be defined in this column. 14 
Cancel condition –  Defines conditions which must be fulfilled to cancel alarm. If filtering time is nee ded, then it must 15 
be defined in this column. 16 
NETCONF Server actions on detection – Defines actions of the NETCONF Server after alarm has been detected. 17 
NETCONF Server actions on cancel – Defines actions of NETCONF Server after alarm has been cancelled. 18 
System recovery actions –  Describes gNB level recovery actions of the NETCONF Client after alarm has b een 19 
indicated by NETCONF Server. This field is informative only; actions taken by the NETCONF Client are not restricted 20 
nor defined in this document. System recovery action “Reset” refers to NETCONF Client forcing reset of O -RU8. 21 
Source – Defines possible sources of the alarm (alarm is within O -RU8). The following are XML encoding provides 22 
examples of the component names defined in various YANG modules that may be alarm sources inside the O-RU8. 23 
- < hardware xmlns= "urn:o-ran:hardware:1.0"><component><o-ran-name/></component></hardware> 24 
- <fan-tray xmlns= "urn:o-ran:fan:1.0"><fan-state><name/></fan-state></fan-tray> 25 
- <sync xmlns= "urn:o-ran:sync:1.0"><gnss-state><name/></gnss-state></sync> 26 
- <external-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:externalio:1.0”><input><name/></input></external-io> 27 
- <external-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:externalio:1.0”><output><name/></output></external-io> 28 
- <ald-ports-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:ald-port:1.0”><ald-port><name/></ald-port></ald-ports-io> 29 
- <port-transceivers xmlns= "urn:o-ran:transceiver:1.0”><port-transceiver-data><name/></ port-30 
transceiver-data ></port-transceivers> 31 
- <interfaces xmlns= "urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:yang:ietf-32 
interfaces”><interface><name/></interface></interfaces> 33 
- <processing-elements xmlns= "urn:o-ran:processing-element.1.0”><ru-elements><name/></ru-34 
elements></processing-elements> 35 
- <-ran-uplane-conf xmlns= "urn:o-ran:uplane-conf.1.0”><low-level-tx-links><name/></low-level-tx-links></ 36 
o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri> 37 
- <o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri xmlns= "urn:o-ran:uplane-conf.1.0”><low-level-rx-links><name/></low-level-rx-38 
links></o-ran-uplane-conf-cpri> 39 
 40 
Note: If Source will not fit to any of above, or is empty, it means that external device (like Antenna Line Devices) cause 41 
an alarm (fault is out of the O -RU8). Then additional text in alarm notification is needed to  clearly say what may be 42 
possible fault source. 43

A parameter: measurement-interval is defined per group of measurement-objects. 5 
A parameter: active is defined per measurement-object. 6 
The object-unit for the measurement-object of rx-window-measurement can be selected per RU, per TRANSPORT, 7 
or EAXC_ID. RU is assumed to support one of the object-units for the rx-window-measurement. 8 
TRANSPORT indicates the name of transport-flow in o-ran-processing-element -cpri YANG. 9 
The type Uint16 is used for EAXC_ID. Measurement result shall contain additional information name for its  10 
transport-flow when EAXC_ID is selected for the object-unit. 11 
A feature "GRANULARITY- EAXC-ID-MEASUREMENT" and a feature "GRANULARITY -TRANSPORT-12 
MEASUREMENT" are defined as optional definition in O-RU8. 13

 2 
A5.1.1 Statistics Calculation 3 
When con figured by the NETCONF client, the O -RU8 captures value of monitored  parameters. Then the O-RU8 4 
calculates x = f(s), where f(s) is a function selected for specific statistics instance. The function f(s) can be one of the 5 
following:  6 
• f(s) = s  7 
• f(s) = LOG10(s),  8 
where LOG10(s) is logarithm with base 10. To avoid issues with  infinity, the O-RU8 assumes that for s < 10 -128 value of 9 
LOG10(s) is -128. 10 
 11 
The value of x = f(s) is applied to first , latest, min and max values; related timestamps are also updated; frequency 12 
table is updated as described in the following section. 13 
 14 
When local measurement interval,  which is not same as transceiver-measurement-interval of the measurement-15 
object, passes the O-RU8 captures value of a monitored parameter (s). Then the O -RU8 calculates x = f(s), where f is a 16 
function selected for specific param eter. The local measurement interval is up to the O -RU8 implementation matter and 17 
typically around 10 sec – 60 sec at earliest. 18 
  19 
The value of x = f(s) is applied to latest value; related timestamp is updated.   20 
The O-RU8 updates statistics:  21 
• If x < min value then x is applied to min value and related timestamp is updated.  22 
• If x > max value then x is applied to max value and related timestamp is updated.  23 
• Value of x is used to update frequency table as described in section Frequency Table below.  24 
 25 
After updates O-RU8 waits another interval to elapse. 26 
 27 
  28 

 O-RAN.WG7.IPC-HRD-Opt8.0-v01.00

the optional capability associated with the model. 6

common control with another entity, so long as such control exists. For the purpose of this Section, 10 
“Control” means beneficial ownership of fifty (50%) percent or more of the voting stock or equity 11 
in an entity. 12 
1.2 “Compliant Implementation” means any system, device, method or operation (whether 13 
implemented in hardware, software or combinations thereof) that fully conforms to a Final 14 
Specification. 15 
1.3 “Adopter(s)” means all entities, who are not Members, Contributors or Academic Contributors, 16 
including their Affiliates, who wish to download, use or otherwise access O-RAN Specifications. 17 
1.4 “Minor Update” means an update or revision to an O-RAN Specification published by O-RAN 18 
ALLIANCE that does not add any significant new features or functionality and remains 19 
interoperable with the prior version of an O-RAN Specification. The term “O-RAN Specifications” 20 
includes Minor Updates. 21 
1.5 “Necessary Claims” means those claims of all present and future patents and patent 22 
applications, other than design patents and design registrations, throughout the world, which (i) are 23 
owned or otherwise licensable by a Member, Contributor or Academic Contributor during the term 24 
of its Member, Contributor or Academic Contributorship; (ii) such Member, Contributor or 25 
Academic Contributor has the right to grant a license without the payment of consideration to a 26 
third party; and (iii) are necessarily infringed by a Compliant Implementation (without considering 27 
any Contributions not included in the Final Specification). A claim is necessarily infringed only 28 
when it is not possible on technical (but not commercial) grounds, taking into account normal 29 
technical practice and the state of the art generally available at the date any Final Specification was 30 
published by the O-RAN ALLIANCE or the date the patent claim first came into existence, 31 
whichever last occurred, to make, sell, lease, otherwise dispose of, repair, use or operate a 32 
Compliant Implementation without infringing that claim. For the avoidance of doubt in exceptional 33 
cases where a Final Specification can only be implemented by technical solutions, all of which 34 
infringe patent claims, all such patent claims shall be considered Necessary Claims. 35
